## Page 131

### [p131_c0001] June 2022 Highlights: Operations Report
### [p131_c0002] East of Hudson
[p131_c0003] 
June East of Hudson service operated above the annual 94% OTP goal at 96.0% OTP, and YTD performance was above goal at 97.2%. All three main lines performed above goal.
[p131_c0004] 
Major Incidents: Four major incidents resulted in 234 delays.
- [p131_c0005] • On June 3 rd , a trespasser incident in the vicinity of Tremont Station on the Harlem line resulted in 27 delays. • On June 4 th and June 22 nd , track circuit issues between CP 113 and 119 on the Harlem Line disrupted service which led to 101 delays. • On June 23 rd , a trespasser strike in the vicinity of Larchmont Station on the New Haven line resulted in 23 delays. • On June 30 th , a track circuit issue between Grand Central Terminal and 125 th Street affected trains arriving and departing Grand Central Terminal. This incident resulted in 83 delays.
### [p131_c0006] West of Hudson
[p131_c0007] 
June West of Hudson service operated above the annual 94% OTP goal at 95.3% OTP, and YTD performance was above goal at 94.1%.
### [p131_c0008] Equipment
[p131_c0009] 
Fleet Availability was at 100% consist compliance for the month, above the goal of 99%.
[p131_c0010] 
In May, Fleet Mean Distance Between Failures was 216,671 miles, 23.8 % higher than the goal of 175,000 miles.
[p131_c0011]

Mean Distance Between Failures (MDBF) is the average number of miles a railcar or locomotive travels in revenue service before breaking down and causing a delay. The higher the MDBF, the more reliable the equipment and the service.

The data shows a general upward trend in MDBF over the period, with a significant peak in December 2021. The 12-month MDBF line shows a slight downward trend after the initial peak in late 2021.

### [p135_c0008] Definitions
[p135_c0009] 
Weekday standees are calculated based on the most recent average weekday customer counts for the train's maximum load point. For Hudson, Harlem and most New Haven Line trains, this point occurs between Harlem-125th St. and the train's next stop outside Manhattan.
[p135_c0010] 
" Program Standees " is the average number of customers in excess of programmed seating capacity.
[p135_c0011] 
" Additional Standees " reflect the impact of reduced train car consists reported as consist compliance less than 100%.
[p135_c0012] 
Note: These statistics do not include the effects of daily ridership variation or uneven distribution of customers within trains. Holidays and Special Events for which there are special equipment programs are not included.
[p135_c0013] 
Operations Planning and Analysis/mk
[p135_c0014]

## Page 142

### [p142_c0001] Metro-North Railroad
### [p142_c0002] June 2022 Highlights: Financial Report
[p142_c0003] 
The Metro-North Railroad's Monthly Financial Report provides year-to-date fiscal information comparing actual revenues, expenses and staffing levels to the Adopted Budget (Budget) and key financial performance indicators. This report presents preliminary 2022 results that are compared and are subject to change pending final year-end accounting adjustments and audit review.
### [p142_c0004] Summary of Non-Reimbursable Year-to-Date (YTD) June 2022 Financial Results
[p142_c0005] 
Ridership and accrual results, versus the Budget, are summarized as follows:
- [p142_c0006] • Ridership of 21.7 million was 90.5% favorable vs. 2021 and 49.1% unfavorable vs. 2019 pre-COVID levels. Ridership was 14.7% unfavorable vs. Budget primarily due to lower commutation ridership. Consequently, farebox revenue of $194.9 million was $25.9 million lower than Budget. • Total revenue of $212.3 million was $22.8 million lower vs. Budget primarily due to lower East of Hudson ridership. • Total expenses of $692.7 million were $3.3 million or 0.5% favorable vs. Budget primarily due to the timing of expenses for materials and maintenance partially offset by higher energy and labor costs.
[p142_c0007] 
Financial results for Year-to-Date (YTD) June 2022 are presented in the table below and compared to the Adopted Budget.
[p142_c0008] 
_MTA Metro-North Railroad June 2022 Year-to-Date Results ($ in Millions)_
[p142_c0009]

## Page 143

### [p143_c0001] NON-REIMBURSABLE and REIMBURSABLE SUMMARY
[p143_c0002] 
June 2022 YTD Net Deficit (Non-Reimbursable and Reimbursable) of $631.4 million was $17.4 million or 2.8% unfavorable vs. the Budget.
[p143_c0003] 
Major drivers of the June 2022 YTD unfavorable result of $17.4 million include lower Non-Reimbursable Revenues of $22.8 million primarily due to lower East of Hudson Revenue.
[p143_c0004] 
June 2022 YTD Reimbursable Expenses of $103.2 million were $41.1 million favorable vs. the Budget due to the scheduling and timing of several projects.
### [p143_c0005] REVENUE/RIDERSHIP
- [p143_c0006] • Farebox Revenue – YTD results were $25.9 million lower vs. the Budget primarily due to lower East of Hudson ridership. ▪ YTD Ridership of 21.7 million was 14.7% unfavorable vs. the Budget, 90.5% favorable vs 2021 and 49.1% unfavorable vs. pre-COVID 2019 levels. • Other Operating Revenue – YTD was $3.2 million favorable vs. the Budget primarily due to higher GCT retail, advertising and parking & stations revenue. • Capital and Other Reimbursements – YTD was $41.1 million or 28.5% unfavorable vs. the Budget primarily due to the scheduling and timing changes of several projects.
### [p143_c0007] TOTAL EXPENSES (Non-Reimbursable and Reimbursable)
[p143_c0008] 
Total Expenses – YTD expenses of $947.0 million were $46.5 million or 4.7% favorable vs. the Budget.
[p143_c0009] 
Labor Expenses (including fringes and overhead recoveries) of $579.0 million YTD were $6.5 million favorable vs. the Budget.
- [p143_c0010] • Payroll – YTD was $16.7 million favorable vs. the Budget primarily due to lower train and engine crew payments as well as the timing of the hiring of vacant positions. • Overtime – YTD was $1.9 million unfavorable vs. the Budget.
[p143_c0011] 
Non-Labor Expenses of $216.9 million YTD were $37.9 million favorable vs. the Budget.
- [p143_c0012] • Electric Power – YTD results were $14.7 million unfavorable vs. the Budget primarily due to higher rates. • Fuel – YTD expenses were $5.5 million unfavorable vs. the Budget primarily due to higher rates. • Maintenance & Other Operating Contracts – YTD was $6.8 million favorable vs. the Budget due to the timing of Non-Reimbursable expenses for BL-20 Locomotive Overhauls, miscellaneous maintenance and operating contracts, and the timing of Reimbursable project activity. • Professional Services – YTD was $10.3 million favorable vs. the Budget due to the timing of Reimbursable project activity and Non-Reimbursable expenses for consulting and engineering services. • Materials & Supplies – YTD was $39.3 million favorable vs. the Budget due to the timing of rolling stock maintenance events, lower rolling stock material usage and the timing of Reimbursable project activity. • Other Business Expenses – YTD was $0.2 million unfavorable vs. the Budget primarily due to higher subsidy payments to New Jersey Transit partially offset by increased Amtrak recoveries and lower credit card processing fees.
[p143_c0013] 
Depreciation and Other Non-Cash Liability Adjustments – YTD were $2.1 million favorable vs. Budget.
[p143_c0014] 
_Master Page # 143 of 170 - Joint Metro-North and Long Island Committees Meeting 7/25/2022_

## Page 144

### [p144_c0001] CASH DEFICIT SUMMARY
[p144_c0002] 
June YTD Net Cash Deficit of $480.4 million was $74.1 million or 18.2% unfavorable to the Budget primarily due to the timing of expenditures for several categories.
### [p144_c0003] FINANCIAL PERFORMANCE MEASURES
- [p144_c0004] • Adjusted Farebox Operating Ratio of 33.4% was 1.8 percentage points unfavorable vs. the Budget. • Adjusted Cost per Passenger of $30.52 was $3.29 unfavorable vs. the Budget. • Revenue per Passenger of $9.00 was $0.30 favorable vs. the Budget.

[p159_c0004] 
(A) Monthly Performance Indicators include both East and West of Hudson revenue and expenses.
[p159_c0005] 
(B) The Standard Farebox Operating Ratio and Cost Per Passenger indicators reflect MTA-wide adopted calculations that exclude non-cash liability adjustments: Depreciation, OPEB Expense (GASB 75), Pension Expense (GASB 68) and Environmental Remediation (GASB-49) as well as the NHL share of MTA Police, Business Service Center and IT costs.
[p159_c0006] 
(C) Adjusted Fare Operating Ratio and Cost Per Passenger indicators have been adjusted for comparability between Metro-North and the LIRR and are being presented only at the railroad operating committees. These adjustments are not being used MTA-wide. Adjustments have been made to reflect all operating revenues and significant financial impacts that are outside management's control. These adjustments include: Inclusion of Other Operating Revenue, Removal of OPEB retiree expenses, and Inclusion of estimated farebox revenue from an equalization of the Connecticut fare structure.

## Page 161

> [p161_c0001] The MTA logo, consisting of the letters 'MTA' in white inside a blue circle.
### [p161_c0002] Metro-North Railroad
### [p161_c0003] June 2022 Highlights: Ridership Report
[p161_c0004] 
(Note: June West of Hudson ridership is preliminary)
### [p161_c0005] June 2022 vs. June 2021
[p161_c0006] 
East of Hudson ridership increased 63.2% vs. June 2021 and was 4.0% below the budget.
- [p161_c0007] • East of Hudson Commutation ridership increased by 166.4%. • East of Hudson Non-Commutation ridership increased by 30.8%.
[p161_c0008] 
East of Hudson Ridership by Line:
- [p161_c0009] • Hudson Line Ridership increased by 60.9%. • Harlem Line Ridership increased by 64.6%. • New Haven Line Ridership increased by 63.3%.
[p161_c0010] 
West of Hudson Ridership by Line:
- [p161_c0011] • Port Jervis Line Ridership increased by 2.9%. • Pascack Valley Line Ridership increased by 0.6%.
### [p161_c0012] June 2022 vs. June 2019
[p161_c0013] 
Total Rail Ridership was 60.5% of 2019 riders.
- [p161_c0014] • East of Hudson ridership decreased by 39.3%. • West of Hudson ridership decreased by 50.3%.
### [p161_c0015] Note:
[p161_c0016] 
Ridership is calculated based on the number of tickets sold multiplied by a factor related to each different type of ticket. The Monthly/Weekly factor is based on the number of weekdays and weekend days per month. June ridership includes Mail & Ride returned and unused refund adjustments.
### [p161_c0017] Ben Cornelius
[p161_c0018] 
Director
[p161_c0019] 
Operations Planning & Analysis
[p161_c0020] 
_Master Page # 161 of 170 - Joint Metro-North and Long Island Committees Meeting 7/25/2022_
